  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

  <span id="freeText10522414523989018183" style="display:none">Claire Danvers has her share of challenges---like being a genius in a school that favors beauty over brains, dealing with the homicidal girls in her dorm, and above all, finding out that her college town is overrun with vampires. On the up side, she has a great roommate (who tends to disappear at sunup) and a new boyfriend named Shane, whose vampire-hunting dad has called in backup: cycle punks who like the idea of killing just about anything.<br /><br />Now a fraternity is throwing its annual Dead Girls' Dance and---surprise!---Claire and her equally outcast best friend, Eve, have been invited. When they find out why, all hell is going to break loose. Because this time both the living and the dead are coming out---and everybody's hungry for blood.</span>

Which is sad, because I really dig YA (I'm a huge Rick Riordan fan, for example), but the characters were flat, the narration kept turning on itself and the dialogue was, to put it mildly, dreadful. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_45910590" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/45910590" />
    <a title="Shannon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2016128-shannon"><img alt="Shannon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572638169p2/2016128.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/45910590?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shannon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shannon" href="/user/show/2016128-shannon">Shannon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=to-sell">to-sell</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer45910590" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9181384362647769001">I don't know what it is about this series that keeps it from being more than average for me. I like the ideas that Caine comes up with but I don't think she's the greatest writer. <b>I find myself distracted while reading her books and not as emotionally connected as I should be.</b> That being said, I liked it enough to want to continue on with the series and find out what happens with the characters.<br/><br/>This entry in the series starts right where the first book left off. This left me feeling a little los</span>
  <span id="freeText9181384362647769001" style="display:none">I don't know what it is about this series that keeps it from being more than average for me. I like the ideas that Caine comes up with but I don't think she's the greatest writer. <b>I find myself distracted while reading her books and not as emotionally connected as I should be.</b> That being said, I liked it enough to want to continue on with the series and find out what happens with the characters.<br /><br />This entry in the series starts right where the first book left off. This left me feeling a little lost though since I read Glass Houses more than a year ago. Fortunately, much of the previous story gets retold in bits and pieces as you read so it's not that hard to remember what had happened. <br /><br />Basically, Shane's Dad is back in town and looking to kill vampires. He gets Claire and the rest of the gang involved and they get in all kinds of trouble. There's some attempted rape, some tortured vampires, and some folded space teleportation. <b>A lot of stuff happens in a short amount of time and it starts to get really unbelievable</b>, especially Claire continually saving the day being a size 2 16 year-old.<br /><br />The only character I really care about is Claire, and she did a lot of stupid things in this book. Actually, Shane, Eve, and Michael all did some stupid things and that's probably one of the reasons I'm having a hard time connecting with them. I do like Shane and Claire's developing romance though.<br /><br /><b>I honestly think Glass Houses and this one should have been made into one book in the first place.</b> And I think that if I had read them back to back I may have enjoyed this one more.<br /><br />Overall, not a bad book, but I'm hoping it improves with the next in the series. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9181384362647769001" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13870608-jo-the-book-sloth?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13870608-jo-the-book-sloth?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer474634136" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16864450134408737444"><b>3.5 I'm Just A Kid Stars</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1412540271i/11388337.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Some days you have to wonder how many enemies can 4 teenagers battle at the same time. As if deadly Vampires and a bunch of psychotic college girls isn't enough, now they have to survive Shane's bat-shit crazy father and his vampire-slaying crusade in a city where no one trusts them and no one is their friend.<br/><br/>Apart from the fact that 4 teenagers manage to do more than a hundred centuries old vampires can do, this series continues to be extremely unique. It gets more gothi</span>
  <span id="freeText16864450134408737444" style="display:none"><b>3.5 I'm Just A Kid Stars</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1412540271i/11388337.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Some days you have to wonder how many enemies can 4 teenagers battle at the same time. As if deadly Vampires and a bunch of psychotic college girls isn't enough, now they have to survive Shane's bat-shit crazy father and his vampire-slaying crusade in a city where no one trusts them and no one is their friend.<br><br>Apart from the fact that 4 teenagers manage to do more than a hundred centuries old vampires can do, this series continues to be extremely unique. It gets more gothic and atmospheric with every page you read and the setting starts to become more and more interesting. The four friends also begin to mature day by day as they come across danger. Sometimes too much danger. Some things seem kind of irrelevant to the story. For example the party scene... I really didn't see its purpose. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The whole rape drug thing did nothing except make Claire look stupid and fill a few pages. I guess the whole massacre at the end was the end purpose but I just thing the issue could have been approached better. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Although admitedly Claire's puppy love for Shane doesn't exactly leave her room to acknowledge when he is behaving like and idiot(which is often), I also like the romance in the series between both couples.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1412540271i/11388338.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The weird thing about these books is that although Claire annoys you with her little girl behaviour, you just can't hold it against her. Sometimes she behaves like an immature little girl and she knows it, she owns it and it is just natural. The girl is barely 16 years old and has to go through things that would break much tougher people. Even when I wanted to kill her, I just couldn't blame her.<br><br>My favorite character in this book though is Amelie by far. She is just so... detached. It's like she's watching everything from a distance. She takes her time in deciding whether she cares or not(most of the times it's "not") and whether or not she will interfere. It's like she has all the time in the world to make her decisions. Of course, when you are the oldest vampire in the world days and human lives probably seem insignificant. She is actually quite badass. More badass than Oliver and his unorganised rage. I actually found it quite naive of Claire to hope that Amelie would help her even though it's quite obvious that Amelie has an interest in Claire.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"Suffice to say that I have chosen to place Shane in that cage for a purpose. He may live, or he may die. That is no longer in my hands, and you may save both your breath and your hopes; I shall not stand up dramatically at the last moment as they light the pyres, and save your lover. Should it come to that, Claire, you must be prepared for the harsh reality that the world is not a fair or just place, and all your wishing cannot make it so. A lesson I learned long, long ago, when the oceans were young, and sand was still rock. I am old, child. Older than you can possibly understand. Old enough that I play with lives like counters in a game. I wish this was not so, but damn me if I can change what I am. What the world is."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1412540271i/11388339.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer172376021431693443"><br/>Dear Series,<br/><br/>I don't know what it is about you, but you confuse me unlike any other series around. <br/><br/>There are times that I like you and I want to get to know you better but then you go and do something stupid to turn me off, only to rekindle my interest in you a few pages later. <br/><br/>It's not fair, dear series. <br/><br/>See, you have this atmospheric-horror-thriller setting going on, keeping me at the edge of my seat, biting my fingernails, and then you send some deus ex machina to do the rescuing.<br/><br/>You give your</span>
  <span id="freeText172376021431693443" style="display:none"><br />Dear Series,<br /><br />I don't know what it is about you, but you confuse me unlike any other series around. <br /><br />There are times that I like you and I want to get to know you better but then you go and do something stupid to turn me off, only to rekindle my interest in you a few pages later. <br /><br />It's not fair, dear series. <br /><br />See, you have this atmospheric-horror-thriller setting going on, keeping me at the edge of my seat, biting my fingernails, and then you send some deus ex machina to do the rescuing.<br /><br />You give your characters depth and flaws and enough layers for me to believe that they could be real, and then you have them react in ways that make no sense whatsoever. <br /><br />I'm trying here, dear series. I want us to be together, I really do, but you've got to be straight with me. If you're gonna be good, be good, if you're not, let me go. No more messing around with my head. <br /><br />Yours Truly<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/626661962" />
    <a title="Anushka" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8377084-anushka"><img alt="Anushka" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452007230p2/8377084.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/626661962?book_show_action=true">May 28, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">No one.</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8377084-anushka?shelf=major-facepalm">major-facepalm</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8377084-anushka?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8377084-anushka?shelf=disappointed">disappointed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8377084-anushka?shelf=overrated">overrated</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8377084-anushka?shelf=everyone-loved-it-but-me">everyone-loved-it-but-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8377084-anushka?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer626661962" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11164231345370916857"><b>I hate the concept.<br/>I hate the characters.<br/>I hate the story line on which this book got off.</b><br/><br/>I practically hate almost everything about this book. So, why did I read this?<br/>I read it 'cause I'm in the mood for reading a series with around 10 books and if anyone can recommend me something better than this, I'll be very grateful.<br/><br/>I read the first part <i> Glass Houses </i> a year back, and disliked it too. The concept is just way too stupid. A 16-year old girl starts going to a college (early admission) in a s</span>
  <span id="freeText11164231345370916857" style="display:none"><b>I hate the concept.<br />I hate the characters.<br />I hate the story line on which this book got off.</b><br /><br />I practically hate almost everything about this book. So, why did I read this?<br />I read it 'cause I'm in the mood for reading a series with around 10 books and if anyone can recommend me something better than this, I'll be very grateful.<br /><br />I read the first part <i> Glass Houses </i> a year back, and disliked it too. The concept is just way too stupid. A 16-year old girl starts going to a college (early admission) in a strange town named Morganville. First, if Claire is such a prodigy, what the hell is she doing studying in <i> Morganville? </i> Couldn't she have gotten a much better college?<br />Then, she starts getting beaten up by the It-girl gang of the school for <b>NO REASON AT ALL.</b> So she leaves her dorm and goes off to live with some random 3 people who are really weird. Those random weird people tell her that the town is run by Vampires and once you've entered it, you can never escape.<br />This plot is <b>dumb as a fucking doorknob.</b><br /><br />There are so many <u>flaws</u> and <u>so much of stupidity</u> in it! To add to this traumatically annoying plot we have the dumbest possible characters. Claire, Eve and Michael are so irritatingly dumb, Shane is okay-okay sometimes. Claire doesn’t ever stands up for herself, she always needs someone to keep her going. Plus, she takes some really rash decisions at times which should make her look like a brave chick, instead it puts her friends in more trouble.<br /><br />I, honestly liked the first one better than <i> Dead Girl’s Dance. </i> The storyline involving Shane’s dad in this instalment was getting on my nerves and it was pretty unnecessary too. I mean, nothing huge happened at the end, everything went back to the way it was before. But in <i> Glass Houses </i> there were a few moments that surprised me and caught my interest (which after a year made me read the 2nd one *rols eyes*). Whereas this one was just <b>dreadful</b>. Everything bored me to death, those <b>good for nothing characters</b> and <b>sissy vampires </b>made me claw my eyes out.<br /><br />I will most probably <b>not</b> continue this series now. My quota of stupidity intake this month is over.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11164231345370916857" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_385163723" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/385163723" />
    <a title="Ian" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6703235-ian"><img alt="Ian" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545987798p2/6703235.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/385163723?book_show_action=true">Aug 06, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ian" href="/user/show/6703235-ian">Ian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer385163723" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer13708595370098687844">At the end of book 1 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27266.Glass_Houses__The_Morganville_Vampires___1_' title='Glass Houses (The Morganville Vampires, #1) by Rachel Caine' rel='nofollow noopener'>Glass Houses</a>, Shane's psychopathic, vampire hunting father and his band of thugs showed up. <i>The Dead Girls' Dance</i> has him running amok in Morganville. The vampires are hunting him and Claire, Shane, Eve and Michael are the meat in the sandwich. <br/><br/>This book has some good things going on, but there are a few things that really annoyed me. The epilogue in the form of diary entries from Eve is tedious. The protagonists spend most of their time whining, and it gets to be a bit much</span>
  <span id="freeText13708595370098687844" style="display:none">At the end of book 1 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27266.Glass_Houses__The_Morganville_Vampires___1_" title="Glass Houses (The Morganville Vampires, #1) by Rachel Caine" rel="nofollow noopener">Glass Houses</a>, Shane's psychopathic, vampire hunting father and his band of thugs showed up. <i>The Dead Girls' Dance</i> has him running amok in Morganville. The vampires are hunting him and Claire, Shane, Eve and Michael are the meat in the sandwich. <br /><br />This book has some good things going on, but there are a few things that really annoyed me. The epilogue in the form of diary entries from Eve is tedious. The protagonists spend most of their time whining, and it gets to be a bit much.<br /> <br />This still would have been a 3.5 star book if it wasn't for this.<br /><br /> <blockquote>
  <i>Claire was feeling kind of light headed, in fact she was dizzy, maybe it was the heat. She took another gulp from the bottle, but that just seemed to make her feel nauseous. <br />As Ian opened the fourth door she said, "I don't feel so good."<br />Ian smiled and said, "Well that was fast", and shoved her into the room. "I thought I was gonna have to work a little harder, but you're pretty easy."<br />There were three other guys in the room...<br /><br />There was something bad out there something worse than four horny, stupid, cruel boys. She felt something brush against her, a hand. One of the boys she didn't know which one, was it Ian? She took it and squeezed.<br /><br />[to Ian, the guy who drugged her and was going to rape her] "I'm sorry about your nose." she said.<br /><br />[later] Those boys weren't monsters.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />OK...so in brief, Ian invites her to the party with the intention of slipping her a drug and then gang-raping her with three of his mates. While defending herself from the would be rapists, she cracks Ian in the nose. Later she apologizes to him for defending herself. They all end up hiding in the closet, and one of the would be rapist takes her hand and she squeezes it. Later she thinks, those guys weren't so bad.<br /><br />WTF!!! On what planet is gang rape not so bad??? That scene is so fucked up and I just can't forgive it. Seriously not cool Ms Caine. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13708595370098687844" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6282699-the-dead-girls-dance">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66639925-amber-j?shelf=5-stars-of-2019">5-stars-of-2019</a>,

<span id="freeTextContainer6120356873331591080"><b>
  <i>“Hess laughed. "You know, I thought you were a mousy little thing when I first saw you, Claire, but you're not, are you? Not underneath."<br/>Oh, I am mousy," she said."All this scares the hell out of me. But I don't know what else to do, sir, except try.<br/>Even a mouse bites.”<br/>― Rachel Caine, The Dead Girls' Dance</i>
</b><br/><br/><i>I try to express only my most honest opinion in a spoiler free way. If you feel anything in my review is a spoiler and is not already hidden in spoiler brackets please let me know. Thank yo</i></span>
  <span id="freeText6120356873331591080" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>“Hess laughed. "You know, I thought you were a mousy little thing when I first saw you, Claire, but you're not, are you? Not underneath."<br />Oh, I am mousy," she said."All this scares the hell out of me. But I don't know what else to do, sir, except try.<br />Even a mouse bites.”<br />― Rachel Caine, The Dead Girls' Dance</i>
</b><br /><br /><i>I try to express only my most honest opinion in a spoiler free way. If you feel anything in my review is a spoiler and is not already hidden in spoiler brackets please let me know. Thank you.</i><br /><p>Shane's dad is in town and on a mission to kill vampires, and he won't let anyone get in his way. Not even his own son. After Shane is accused of the crime his dad commited. Claire, Eve, and Micheal have to find some way to save him. They make some allies along the way and a lot of enemies.</p><br /><p>Loved it!!! This series is amazing. I can't believe I haven't heard more about it. I know its a bit on the older side, but still. This would make a great series I think or a long movie series. It reads like one and I love it. I love that there are still 13 more books to read in this series and that doesn't even include the companion books. I will say though that there is a part in the book that I sooo saw coming. *Spoiler Alert* <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ So at about 3/4 of the way through when Claire and Eve were at the party and Claire drank the water bottle that was handed to her OPENED by a guy she barely knew. I immediately started yelling at my book, I knew it was coming. 16 years old in college early and her parents didn't think to remind her to watch her drinks at a party? That part had me in a bit of a rage lol. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> </p><br /><p>
  <i>How I choose my rating:<br />1* Did not finish, or hated it but forced myself to finish.<br />2** Didn't really like it. Didn't hate it but not sure why I finished it other then for some closure.<br />3*** I liked it. I had some issues with it, but as a whole it was good. I probably won't reread again ever, but there is a chance I might finish the series. (If part of one) But if not it's not a huge loss.<br />4**** I really liked this book. Maybe not a work of genius, but highly entertaining. I might reread this again, and I will finish the series. (If part of one) I would recommend to those I know hold interest in this books content.<br />5***** I loved this book. I found little to no issues with it at all. I will definitely be rereading this and probably more than once. I will finish the series and reread it multiple times. (If part of one) I will recommend this book to EVERYONE!!!!</i>
</p></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Lissa Smith Reads&#39;~Bookaholics Bookshelf Reviews" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Lissa Smith Reads&#39;~Bookaholics Bookshelf Reviews" href="/user/show/5324453-lissa-smith-reads-bookaholics-bookshelf-reviews"> Lissa Smith Reads&#39;~Bookaholics Bookshelf Reviews</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer171327242" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer179640614856178300"><b>5 Stars:</b> <br/>This story was even more intense than Glass Houses. It was full of emotions throughout the whole book. Claire's decision at the book's end is heartbreaking, but so in character for her. This book was so much better than the last one. Not to disappointed as of yet, and I am not going on a rambling tyrant reveling any details as I did with Glass House. Sorry you will have to read and enjoy for yourself.<br/><br/>My absolute favorite and will read again and again. I strongly recommend! It has outsta</span>
  <span id="freeText179640614856178300" style="display:none"><b>5 Stars:</b> <br />This story was even more intense than Glass Houses. It was full of emotions throughout the whole book. Claire's decision at the book's end is heartbreaking, but so in character for her. This book was so much better than the last one. Not to disappointed as of yet, and I am not going on a rambling tyrant reveling any details as I did with Glass House. Sorry you will have to read and enjoy for yourself.<br /><br />My absolute favorite and will read again and again. I strongly recommend! It has outstanding qualities. The characters are wonderful and surprising and multi-dimensional. The writing is luring, engaging, and well-crafted enough to keep me interested from cover to cover and beyond. The plot is astonishing with twists and turns weaved into a well thought and planned story. There’s no pretense and romance was well balanced and done entirely correctly with properly distributed amounts of hints, behaviors and incredible, undeniable chemistry. Predictability is at an all-time low. With the exception of series based books that follow the same path but are just as good. <b>
  <i>Overall, Favorite, must read again, recommend!!!</i>
</b></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7923799578011947454">The Dead Girls' Dance is the second book in the Morganville Vampire series and it picks up right after the ending of the first book. Claire and her roommates now not only have the vampires to deal with in Morganville but Shane's father has shown up with his bikers buddies. <br/><br/>So far I'm finding this series just rather average. Sometimes I enjoy what's going on but at other times I find Claire to be rather annoying and some of the choices made to be laughable. I'm still kind of comparing this to som</span>
  <span id="freeText7923799578011947454" style="display:none">The Dead Girls' Dance is the second book in the Morganville Vampire series and it picks up right after the ending of the first book. Claire and her roommates now not only have the vampires to deal with in Morganville but Shane's father has shown up with his bikers buddies. <br /><br />So far I'm finding this series just rather average. Sometimes I enjoy what's going on but at other times I find Claire to be rather annoying and some of the choices made to be laughable. I'm still kind of comparing this to some of the rather campy horror movies that are usually more for a laugh but that's not necessarily a bad thing either. <br /><br />Not really a bad read but room for improvement still. Hoping that Claire will mature a bit in the upcoming books. Things should get a bit more interesting after some of the happenings in this book. <br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1121573-samantha?shelf=2009">2009</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1121573-samantha?shelf=ebook-own">ebook-own</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer46537621&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer46537621" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13508344983114551511">Ok, I decided to read this 2nd installment after liking the first, even with a few reservations. TDGD has not added anything new to the mix for me. I'll list my arguments:<br/><br/><br/><br/>1. Claire has known Shane, Eve, and Michael for less than a month and she's willing to sign her life away. I'm not saying love is measured by how long you know someone, but come on! She's 16!<br/><br/>2. This girl has dreams of going to MIT (=eventually leaving town) when she just keeps on digging deeper into this town's secrets when she</span>
  <span id="freeText13508344983114551511" style="display:none">Ok, I decided to read this 2nd installment after liking the first, even with a few reservations. TDGD has not added anything new to the mix for me. I'll list my arguments:<br /><br /><br /><br />1. Claire has known Shane, Eve, and Michael for less than a month and she's willing to sign her life away. I'm not saying love is measured by how long you know someone, but come on! She's 16!<br /><br />2. This girl has dreams of going to MIT (=eventually leaving town) when she just keeps on digging deeper into this town's secrets when she knows people have been killed for less. She's never going anywhere and frankly that's just depressing, especially since she can't see it.<br /><br />3. This book is about teenagers, I get that. Teenagers just aren't going to have much say in the rules. It just gets really old watching everything happen TO them. If you think about the grand scheme of the story they really aren't the people you want to hear more about.<br /> <br />Book plot consists of: have a nice happy dinner together = Claire and/or Eve to Michael and/or Shane "You can't tell me what to do!" = C&amp;E either get locked in a room or leave and get caught (repeat 3 or 4 times) = vampire comes along makes big appearance and they live to see another dinner of chili or tacos.<br /><br />GETS OLD! Needless to say I probably won't continue with this series.<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

          </span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer19922573" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer145484542053068826">This is the second book in the Morganville Vampire series and it picks up right where book one leaves off. By now, we've learned a bit more about all the inhabitants of the Glass House, where Claire is currently living off-campus while attending Texas Prarie University. Her roommates—Eve the Goth girl, sexy hunk Shane, and mysterious Michael—have been having to fight off the vampires that rule Morganville because situations beyond their control have really pissed some of them off. It certainly d</span>
  <span id="freeText145484542053068826" style="display:none">This is the second book in the Morganville Vampire series and it picks up right where book one leaves off. By now, we've learned a bit more about all the inhabitants of the Glass House, where Claire is currently living off-campus while attending Texas Prarie University. Her roommates—Eve the Goth girl, sexy hunk Shane, and mysterious Michael—have been having to fight off the vampires that rule Morganville because situations beyond their control have really pissed some of them off. It certainly doesn't help when Shane's vampire-hunting father comes to town either, with a plan to take care of all the vampires of Morganville once and for all.<br /><br />If I hadn't read the first book so recently I think I may have been lost for the first several pages as this book picks up mid-scene from the events of book one, with very little reminder cues. I really don't like when authors do this, particularly since these books are published several months apart and most people aren't going to read them right after another, but instead would read a number of other books in betweeen. Therefore, with this particular series, you might be better served picking up the first two or three books and then reading them all in one go.<br /><br />In comparison to the other young adult urban (paranormal) fantasy books I've been reading, specifically the House of Night Novels by P.C. Cast, these seem a bit slower paced and not nearly as exciting. I remember thinking something similar about the first book of Ms. Caine's Weather Warden series, <i>Ill Wind</i>, when I read that. Certainly an interesting enough story, but it didn't have that wow factor for me that makes it a favorite. *shrug*<br /><br />That said, the story is still interesting enough to keep going, and does pick up the pace more as things progress. Though written in the third person, you really only see into Claire's head most of the time, not any of the other main characters, so the inclusion of a few excerpts from Eve's diary at the end of the book is a welcome addition which lets you learn a bit more about what makes her tick. <br /><br />I certainly plan to keep up with future books in this series, and already have <i>Midnight Alley</i>, the third in the series, waiting on my bookshelf. I'll just have to remember to read it sooner rather than later for the reasons stated above since I'll be passing this second book along and won't have it to refer back to.</span>
  <a data-text-id="145484542053068826" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17684223727052705605">Complete waste of my time. <br/>I can't believe I wasted a second of my life in this series. <br/>Sure, I liked Glass House even though I was ready to tear my hair out if I had to read one more fucking page of that book.<br/>But here?<br/>I couldn't even finish it.<br/>Wanna know the reason why I read this? <br/>The fucking cliffhanger.<br/>Man, I hate those thing, they're pure evil.<br/><br/>Anyways, I kinda have to thank this book because I realized this series annoyed me to no end.   <span id="freeText17684223727052705605" style="display:none">Complete waste of my time. <br />I can't believe I wasted a second of my life in this series. <br />Sure, I liked Glass House even though I was ready to tear my hair out if I had to read one more fucking page of that book.<br />But here?<br />I couldn't even finish it.<br />Wanna know the reason why I read this? <br />The fucking cliffhanger.<br />Man, I hate those thing, they're pure evil.<br /><br />Anyways, I kinda have to thank this book because I realized this series annoyed me to no end. I just wanted to skip to the end and get it over with. And not in the 'omg! I wanna know what happens next!' way but in the 'can we just get this over with? God my eyes are bleeding and I'm just about to bash my head so I can get outta here' way.<br />I would have chucked it at my wall but I was reading an e-copy, so, no.<br />I think the only reason the first book was bearable was Shane, even though he really isn't that great of a guy. I can deal with Claire's crying, but I cannot deal with stupidity. She was supposed to be the smart one, wasn't she? Well, in this book I just couldn't see that.<br />I'm sorry Claire, but you are just useless. Sure, you memorized the elements of the periodic table and their reactions, but when its about serious decisions? <br />You are as useless as a spoon is to open a can.<br /><br />I won't continue this series (as if that isn't obvious) and I definitely won't recommend this to anyone—well, maybe my mortal enemy but that's it. <br />I am so done.<br />Camila out.<br />Carpe diem!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16457888321440235808">This wasn't as funny as the first book, but it still kept me involved. There was a lot of plot progression, but not a massive amount of character development. We get to know more about Morganville, and about Shane's past, but it was hard to feel very empathetic as he was absent through a large chunk of the book. This series is very episodic, which makes it hard to put down. It's fluff. But it's fun fluff.</span>

  <span id="freeText14709364889210696958" style="display:none">I feel like as this series is continuing we are getting sucked farther and farther into the supernatural world. They will never be able to get out of this place. This town is definitely messed up with what they allow to happen. Luckily we pick up here right where book 1 leaves off. This is a good thing especially with the cliffhanger of the last book!<br /><br />Claire and crew step off into even more trouble as Shane's dad has shown back up. We get to really learn about Shane's past which is even more tragic than we first thought, Monica is up to some very awful shenanigans and still hasn't got hers.. at least not enough for me to feel satisfied. Shane gets accused of some crimes he didn't commit in an effort to get rid of both him and his dad. Eve is having her own family issues turning up and Michael gets an opportunity to finally have a life... kinda.<br /><br />This series so far has been almost a little too YA to really keep my interest. I keep thinking if Claire and crew would just grown up a little more it wouldn't be so bad. Maybe they would quit heading straight into danger with no thoughts to consequences whatsoever. The barely making it out of these situations is really riding my anxiety lol. I wonder what is up next for the crew?</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer302610121351811252">I'm a bit surprised at how fast things are happening? I thought some of the really important plot points in <i>The Dead Girls' Dance</i> happened later in the series, but I guess not. Still a v entertaining and fast read, filled with action and danger and Claire getting hurt and then sleeping it off and waking up all healed \o/<br/><br/>The book begins right where the last one left off and also sets up quite a few important plot points for the next installments in the series. One of them does get kind of brushed</span>
  <span id="freeText302610121351811252" style="display:none">I'm a bit surprised at how fast things are happening? I thought some of the really important plot points in <i>The Dead Girls' Dance</i> happened later in the series, but I guess not. Still a v entertaining and fast read, filled with action and danger and Claire getting hurt and then sleeping it off and waking up all healed \o/<br /><br />The book begins right where the last one left off and also sets up quite a few important plot points for the next installments in the series. One of them does get kind of brushed off in this book in favor of Frank Collins being the worst human, but I know it'll be picked up again later on. Also, not a lot of development with Claire and Shane's romance; it's definitely going to be a slow burn kind of thing since Caine focuses a lot on Claire still being underage.<br /><br />Warning this time for two attempted rape scenes, past mentions of drug addiction, referenced/implied physical abuse, and referenced/implied child sexual abuse. Claire's inner monologue also likes to reinforce heteronormative stereotypes so, you know, yikes.</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2406353-rachel-the-rest-is-still-unwritten?shelf=i-own">i-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer63958162&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer63958162" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1100425279586853021">This book was equally as good as the first. <br/>The story picked up right where the first book left of and continued to be fast paced and entertaining the entire way through. <br/>The characters continue to be the same great personalities they were from the first book, and I really liked Sam. I feel like he may be the first vampire we’ve met who could be as close to good as vampires in this series can get. I really like the character of Amelie, although I wonder exactly what her intentions are and just h</span>
  <span id="freeText1100425279586853021" style="display:none">This book was equally as good as the first. <br />The story picked up right where the first book left of and continued to be fast paced and entertaining the entire way through. <br />The characters continue to be the same great personalities they were from the first book, and I really liked Sam. I feel like he may be the first vampire we’ve met who could be as close to good as vampires in this series can get. I really like the character of Amelie, although I wonder exactly what her intentions are and just how far she’ll go to get what she wants. Who and what would she be willing to risk in order to protect herself? <br />Personally I think both Claire and Shane along with Eve and Michael are great couples. One of the things that struck me about this series straight away, is how there doesn’t appear to be any love triangles. Honestly, I’ve become sick of them and seeing two fresh couples who are all close and get along together without any extra issues is excellent. It’s a breath of fresh air and I hope it stays that way. I don’t want to see anyone pop up in the story that could be a threat to either romance. <br /><br />I like that Claire continues to grow and appears to becoming stronger. It’s wonderful when the main character continues to evolve over the course of the series. I find that she’s very mature for her age too. Often during the book, I found myself forgetting that she is almost two years younger than her housemates. She’s very level and balanced that it’s hard to think of her as a child. <br />I find it very difficult to define Shane after this book. He’s not exactly a bad-boy, although he has that hint of rebelliousness that makes him fun and he’s not outright innocent or sweet either. After learning of his father, it’s obvious that he’s done a number on Shane over the years and that in a lot of ways Shane is vulnerable when it comes to his dad. He’s the only family Shane has left and while doesn’t completely agree or disagree with his father’s beliefs on vampires; Shane can’t deny that he’s a part of that world. Or was. At the end of the book Shane made it obvious how little he wanted to do with his father, but I wonder how long that will last. <br />I thought it was very interesting to see Michael become a vampire. If there is anyone who can become one of the unread and yet manage to hold on to his humanity and still be himself, it’s him. <br />Also I wonder how Eve’s brother Jason is going to affect the storyline. Is he really the one killing those girls? And will he be in the next book? <br /><br />I’m looking forward to finding out. <br />Now, on to the next book......<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1100425279586853021" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2348288868" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11113800507824551068"><p>This book picks up right where <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3566345.Glass_Houses__The_Morganville_Vampires___1_' title='Glass Houses (The Morganville Vampires, #1) by Rachel Caine' rel='nofollow noopener'>Glass Houses</a> left off, with the aftermath of <i>that</i> cliffhanger. We've got ourselves a new villain in the form of Frank Collins - Shane's father - but that doesn't mean the old ones are going away. <b>The Glass House gang still find themselves in the middle of trouble, which, honestly, could be a summary of the entire series.</b></p><p>Since this is a reread, I'm aware of the fact that this book is setting up a lot of important events, and introducing characters that play a bigger</p></span>
  <span id="freeText11113800507824551068" style="display:none"><p>This book picks up right where <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3566345.Glass_Houses__The_Morganville_Vampires___1_" title="Glass Houses (The Morganville Vampires, #1) by Rachel Caine" rel="nofollow noopener">Glass Houses</a> left off, with the aftermath of <i>that</i> cliffhanger. We've got ourselves a new villain in the form of Frank Collins - Shane's father - but that doesn't mean the old ones are going away. <b>The Glass House gang still find themselves in the middle of trouble, which, honestly, could be a summary of the entire series.</b></p><p>Since this is a reread, I'm aware of the fact that this book is setting up a lot of important events, and introducing characters that play a bigger part in the series as a whole. That isn't all this book does however - it has its own plot, and we learn more about our characters as they continue to develop and reveal things about their past.</p><p><b>Perhaps my favourite thing that happens in this book is the introduction of Sam</b> - Morganville's youngest (and sweetest) vampire. There's also more of Richard - Monica's cop brother - who I love for the simple fact that he's constantly fed up with everyone and everything around him.</p><p>While I do think <b>this is one of the less memorable books in the series, it's definitely worth reading</b>, both for the important things that happen and the developments between characters. It doesn't hold the same place in my heart as <i>Glass Houses</i>, but <i>The Dead Girls' Dance</i> is a good continuation of the series.</p></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3167178-shera-book-whispers?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3167178-shera-book-whispers?shelf=vampire">vampire</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3167178-shera-book-whispers?shelf=ebook-second">ebook-second</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3167178-shera-book-whispers?shelf=2007">2007</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer85440245" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16607348715665071720">Well it was better than the first book. I think the characters and plot development hit the right spots. We get to know more about everyone, and with the books being so small that is an issue. There's a limited time to developed characters and the world, while trying to squeeze in the plots! Dead Girls' Dance does a better job of it. <br/><br/>Though my real issues where how Claire handled the situations. Despite Monica, the mean (psycho) girl, trying to kill her in the last book Claire just kind of shrug</span>
  <span id="freeText16607348715665071720" style="display:none">Well it was better than the first book. I think the characters and plot development hit the right spots. We get to know more about everyone, and with the books being so small that is an issue. There's a limited time to developed characters and the world, while trying to squeeze in the plots! Dead Girls' Dance does a better job of it. <br /><br />Though my real issues where how Claire handled the situations. Despite Monica, the mean (psycho) girl, trying to kill her in the last book Claire just kind of shrugs it off. I don't understand. Not to mention that rape was used as a plot device to get readers blood going. Then it wasn't handled well. Those boys should have been reported properly. I wanted to see it. Not just threatened by a vampire. <br /><br />Not to mention that things just happen. Claire and company don't think things through. It worked out better here. But it still annoyed me. Yes things just happen and you have no control. <br /><br />In the end this book finally got me connecting to the characters. It reminded me why I loved them so much. All of the little nuances I'm picking up are a fun look back for moments I still remember happening in the later books. Not to mention that I love Shane, Eve, Claire, and Michael. They are a fun group to be around. Lots happens, but at least the cliffhanger isn't so cruel! The entire book is a rush and I'm looking forward to the next one. <br /><br /><b>Sexual Content:</b> Making out, smooching, and some adult thoughts. Sexual humor, check. As mentioned there was some rape issues. Things didn't go too far, but there were drugs involved. It also emphasized how seemingly nice guys become monsters. <br /> <br /><b>3/5- Adored it, just a few minor details held it back.</b><br /><br /><b>
  <i>Originally reviewed at <a href="http://www.shera-bookwhispers.blogspot.com/2016/03/review-dead-girls-dance.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Whispers</a>.</i>
</b><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16607348715665071720" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('UXAVMUhhMOOFmxrkrVdgBqkCSX0aE5rJPzgsIIj5ErlrVnzj8z/5iyKwroVaomrZf12utdSeFK5kRmqRRbrgIw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('poRvVxuaUvueiezjqIlj3mpcK9aY7Vb3/sChxlTMCaecogaFoMSbkzmiWIJffGkBvAPMHlZg2JClvud3mY/7PQ==')})
  }
